New York Heavyweight Boxing Championship: Wagner and Xia Gai Tie

丨The result of fifteen rounds of hard work丨

New York, 22nd telegram The local boxing association, after expressing its dissent regarding the German Schmering holding onto the heavyweight boxing championship this year, started anew and held a match between Mai Gai Wagner and Jack Xia Gai on the evening of July 22 at the Aibola Arena in Broukelun. There were 25,000 enthusiastic spectators participating in this scene of a dragon and tiger fight. Fifteen rounds went by, and the two were equally matched, resulting in a tie.

▲ The entry of the two heroes shook the earth.

丨Xia Gai weighed 29 pounds more丨

▲ Wagner makes a comeback Wagner, the world middleweight boxing champion, had won every battle before his retirement, maintaining his reputation undefeated. When he declared his leap into the heavyweight boxing stage, boxing experts generally gave him good sympathy. As reported in yesterday's newspaper, McOlifu, the retired lightweight champion, even promised him to be a future championship winner. His popularity can be seen. His weight is 169 and a half pounds.

▲ Xia Gai is full of heroism Jack Xia Gai, when he competed with Schmering for hegemony last year, was on a roll, but was judged to have failed due to a foul. Commentators regretted it. Afterwards, Xia Gai was unwilling to accept and requested a rematch. Xue refused. The New York Committee then reversed and recognized Xia Gai as the champion. His weight is 198 and a half pounds, which is 29 pounds heavier than Wagner, which is quite an advantage. When the two heroes entered the arena with tiger-like steps, they were greeted by enthusiastic cheers from the crowd, shaking the earth. It was a grand event for a time.

▲ Fifteen rounds of competition: crowned kings side by side

丨Most of the audience at the arena praised Wagner丨

▲ Xia Gai launches a strong attack At the beginning of the match, Xia Gai was cautious and repeatedly forced Wagner to the side of the rope. His left and right hands kept circling and advancing. Wagner's defense was thorough, and he was spared injury. In the first and second rounds, Xia Gai launched a strong attack and gained the upper hand.

▲ Wagner gradually gains the upper hand In the third and fourth rounds, Xia Gai was defeated. In the fourth round, Xia Gai tried hard to trap Wagner in a dead end, placing both fists horizontally in front of his chest and exposing his face completely to lure the enemy to attack, and then taking the opportunity to attack. However, Wagner advanced and retreated well, and did not fall into the enemy's trap. Although Wagner repeatedly won in these two rounds, he only had a slight advantage.

▲ Xia Gai injures the enemy and benefits From the fifth round, Xia Gai struck fiercely, and Wagner fell to the ground, but he immediately jumped up without any injury. Soon after, Wagner's eye was injured, and he lost the fifth, sixth, and seventh rounds as a result. The eighth round was a tie because Xia Gai was ultimately unable to break through Wagner's defense.

▲ Wagner strives to be promising In the ninth round, the two men fought wildly against each other. Then, Wagner repeatedly hit the enemy's stomach, causing Xia Gai to sway. Wagner won this round. In the next tenth round, there was no distinction between the two.

▲ The situation is unpredictable In the eleventh round, Wagner continued to take the offensive. Xia Gai was hit and swayed as if drunk. Wagner took the upper hand again. In the twelfth round, Xia Gai punched the enemy in the face, and Wagner's face was covered in blood. Thanks to his effective defense, although he lost this round, the overall situation was not affected.

▲ The two divide the honors equally In the fourteenth round, Xia Gai always thought of knocking down the enemy with one blow, but the enemy was good at defending. In the fifteenth round, the three worked even harder, but one was hard and one was soft, one was clumsy and one was skillful, and the two rounds ended in a tie. It was difficult to judge who was strong and who was weak.

▲ The crowd praises Wagner Wagner performed his lifelong best, not giving Xia Gai any slight advantage. Therefore, he was greatly praised by the crowd. Xia Gai seemed surprised by this challenger. After the three referees voted, Daonawan nominated Wagner, one nominated Xia Gai, and the third cast a peaceful vote. The battle closed, and the two were declared crowned kings side by side.

Nanyang Summer School Basketball Team Wins Shangzhong

The Nanyang Commercial High School Summer School basketball team went to the Provincial Shanghai Middle School yesterday afternoon at 4:00 to play a friendly match with the Shangzhong Summer School basketball team. As a result, Nanyang won with a score of 39 to 18, it was judged.

Song Ziwen's Encounter with Danger at the North Station Yesterday Morning

▲ Assailants and Guards Exchange Fire

▲ Minister Song Escapes Danger with Alertness

▲ Secretary Tang Yuluo Tragically Dies

▲ One Guard and Ten Passengers Injured

▲ Assailants Flee, One Suspect Apprehended

Finance Minister Song Ziwen, accompanied by his confidential secretary Tang Yuluo and six guards, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:00 AM from Nanjing on the overnight express train. After Song and his party alighted from the train and walked out of the platform into the station hall, passing the information desk and reaching the waiting room entrance, a group of assailants suddenly appeared. They pulled out hand grenades, Mauser pistols, and handguns and launched a fierce attack on Song. Song's guards also drew their guns and returned fire. Bullets flew in all directions, and smoke filled the air. The North Station hall was instantly transformed into a battlefield. At the time, passengers were crowding to exit the station and scattered in panic at the sound of gunfire, throwing everything into chaos. As a result, Mr. Song was fortunate to escape unharmed, but Secretary Tang Yuluo sustained three gunshot wounds and died from his injuries at 11:30 AM yesterday. One of Song's guards sustained minor injuries, and ten other passengers were wounded by stray bullets, including Wang Shiduo, a secretary of the Control Yuan with the rank of senior appointee. The details obtained by our newspaper reporter from the investigation are recorded below:

Column at the North Station Hall Marked with Bullet Holes (Photo by This Newspaper)

Song and Tang Walked Side by Side: The Nanjing-Shanghai overnight train is scheduled to arrive at the North Station at 6:53 AM. Yesterday morning, the train arrived at 7:08 AM, a delay of fifteen minutes. Mr. Song was riding in the private car at the rear of the train. After getting off, he emerged from the platform in the crowd. At the time, Inspector Zhao Xinzhong, dispatched by the station police department, was leading the way with two officers. Mr. Song was wearing a Western-style suit, an overcoat, and a white foreign cloth helmet. He walked side by side with Secretary Tang. Tang was wearing a summer cloth long gown and carrying a large black leather bag. Behind Song and Tang were Song's six guards.

Portrait of Mr. Tang Yuluo

▲ Assailants Lay in Ambush: As Song and his party walked past the station information desk at the east entrance of the hall and advanced a few more steps, about seven or eight assailants, who had concealed themselves by the large cement columns, suddenly pulled out their guns and fired at Song. Several loud bangs rang out, and the scene instantly changed. The time was 7:12 AM. Song's guards quickly drew their guns and returned fire. The assailants then threw hand grenades, creating bright flashes and dense smoke. Mr. Song, with his quick wits, quickly threw away his white hat and also ducked behind a large column. The guards surrounded and protected him from the front and rear, but Secretary Tang became the target of the attack and instantly fell to the ground, wounded. At the same time, Song was escorted by railway police to the traffic office and rested in the office of the two bureau chiefs on the second floor. Meanwhile, the remaining guards continued to engage in a fierce battle with the assailants. The two sides fired no less than a hundred bullets. After about five minutes, the assailants, not daring to linger, hastily abandoned their weapons and escaped into the crowd of passengers, disappearing without a trace.

▲ Tang Sent to Hospital: After the assailants fled and the gunfire gradually subsided, the injured Secretary Tang was quickly helped into Mr. Song's car by the guards and taken to Baolong Hospital for treatment. They arrived at the hospital at 7:25 AM. At the same time, Minister Song, in the bureau chief's office, urgently notified the Garrison Headquarters by telephone, requesting that troops be dispatched to provide protection. At 7:40 AM, Song himself, accompanied by his guards, returned to his residence in his own car that had come back from Baolong Hospital, to rest. Among Song's party, besides Tang, who sustained three gunshot wounds, and one guard, Min Ziqing, whose left leg was hit by shrapnel from a hand grenade, the rest were unharmed, which was indeed fortunate.

▲ Severe Bladder Injury: The guard Min Ziqing, 32 years old, from Hubei, was injured in the right leg by shrapnel and immediately collapsed to the ground, unable to stand. After Song and his party returned to their residence, a car was hired by the railway police to first take Min to his residence in Zhabei. At around 9:00 AM, he was also sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment. After Secretary Tang arrived at the hospital, his family members rushed to visit him. His cousin, Xu Zhendong, telegraphed Niu Huisheng to come and provide medical treatment. At 8:20 AM, Dr. Niu arrived at the hospital with Dr. Cao Chentao. However, Dr. Bader from Baolong Hospital had not yet arrived by 8:40 AM. At the time, Dr. Niu immediately believed that surgery was imperative and could not be delayed any longer. At 8:45 AM, he was transported to the Red Cross Society on Haige Road for treatment. It was found that Tang had sustained three gunshot wounds: two in his right arm and one in his bladder. The bladder wound was the most serious, and the bullet was still lodged inside.

▲ Dies Yesterday Afternoon: Surgery was performed immediately on his lower abdomen, and it was discovered that his bladder had been pierced in three places, which were repaired. However, the bullet could not be removed. When Tang was at Baolong Hospital, his spirits were still good, and he was still conscious. However, after the surgery, his temperature suddenly rose at around 11:00 AM. At 11:30 AM, he succumbed to his injuries and could not be saved. His family members quickly moved his body to the Universal Funeral Parlor and scheduled the funeral for this Saturday (the 25th).

▲ Mr. Tang's Brief Biography: Tang Yuluo was 32 years old and a native of Jinhua, Zhejiang. In 1920, he graduated from Harvard University in the United States, majoring in economics and earning a master's degree. After returning to China, he served as a secretary for Feng Yuxiang and later became the chief editor of the English-language "Continental Daily News" in Shanghai. When Qian Dajun served as the Songhu Garrison Commander, Tang served as his secretary. Tang had served as a secretary in the Ministry of Finance for three years, working in the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Finance. He was recently promoted to confidential secretary and was highly trusted by Minister Song. Tang accompanied Song on his trips between Nanjing and Shanghai. Just last week, Tang accompanied Song to Nanjing. He returned to Shanghai with Song yesterday morning, a matter of only two days.

▲ Newly Married for Two Months: Mr. Tang was the brother of the socialite Tang Ying. His father, Tang Naian, passed away two years ago. Mr. Tang married the niece of the late Executive Yuan President Tan Yankai just two months ago. He lived at No. 39 Route Dufour, with only an elderly mother and no brothers. Yesterday afternoon, when the tragic news arrived, his wife was grief-stricken and fainted repeatedly. She was revived by medical attention. The whole house was filled with cries, a truly tragic scene. Guo Dehua, Secretary of the Ministry of Finance, and Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, personally went to offer their condolences.

▲ Number of Injured: Yesterday morning, in addition to Tang Yufu, who died, a total of ten people were wounded by gunshots. The details are listed as follows: (1) Wang Shiduo, a secretary of the Control Yuan with the rank of senior appointee, injured in the right foot by a hand grenade, at Fumin Hospital; (2) Min Ziqing, a guard of Song Ziwen, injured in the right leg by a hand grenade, at Baolong Hospital; (3) Wang Xifang, gunshot wound to the right foot, currently the supply director of the 33rd Independent Brigade, at Baolong Hospital; (4) Zhang A'gen, 54 years old, from Suzhou, bullet entered from the back and exited from the left waist, perforated colon, life in critical condition, at Renji Hospital; (5) Zhang Zhenxiang, 36 years old, from Nanxiang, gunshot wound to the right ear; (6) Lin Jingfang, 27 years old, adjutant of the 8th Regiment of the 2nd Guard Division, Cantonese, picked up a bomb, four fingers of his right hand were blown off, and his face was injured, at Renji Hospital; (7) Ding Xueyuan, 21 years old, from Hubei, guard soldier, gunshot wound to the head, at Renji Hospital; (8) Liu Baoqing, 40 years old, grocery store owner, bullet in the buttocks, at Renji Hospital; (9) Zheng Jinian, railway police officer, hand grenade injury to the lower jaw; (10) Zhu Yuwen, 32 years old, rickshaw puller, bullet grazed the right eye. It is said that there were at least a dozen others who sustained minor injuries from stray bullets and went to various hospitals for treatment on their own.

▲ Weapons Recovered: After the incident, the police department of the two railways recovered a Mauser pistol, two Brownings, and a hand grenade from the hall. The Mauser pistol still had two bullets in it. All were sent to the Fifth District Police Station for safekeeping. Yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM, Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, went to the station to inspect and retrieved the weapons from the Fifth District Police Station for reference. In addition, a handgun with seven bullets inside was also recovered by Chinese and foreign detectives from the side of the border road near the iron shed opposite the station and stored in the Huikuisi police station.

▲ Hand Grenade Explosion: At 8:17 AM, railway police officers were re-investigating the area and found a handkerchief-wrapped object stuffed into a crack in the western iron shed. They suspected it was an explosive device placed there by the assailants. Railway police officer Zheng Jiyuan was stationed to guard it, waiting for a way to safely remove and destroy it. Unexpectedly, Lin Jingfang, a Cantonese adjutant from the 8th Regiment of the 4th Brigade of the National Government Guard Army, who had come to Shanghai from Nanjing on the night train, passed by the area after disembarking from the train. Upon hearing people say that the package contained a bomb, Lin bent down to pick it up. Although Officer Zheng advised him not to take the risk, Lin, relying on his long experience in battle, was not afraid of firearms. He still reached out to take it, saying it was to prevent harm to others. As soon as he reached out, a loud explosion went off inside the package. Four fingers of Lin's hand, which had taken the package, were blown off, and his left hand, chest, and face were all injured. The lower jaw of railway police officer Zheng Jiyuan was also injured by shrapnel. A rickshaw puller named Zhu Yuwen, who was passing by at the time, was also affected and injured in the corner of his eye.

▲ Temporary Martial Law: When the bombs exploded and the gunfire rang out, passengers in the station scrambled to escape, and the order was quite chaotic. Passengers on the Routes 5 and 6 trams stopped at the border road also got off and fled at the sound of the gunfire. Rumors flew everywhere. The concession police station dispatched a large number of armed detectives to the border road and imposed temporary martial law. Soldiers from the Sixth Division of the Fifth Army also stood guard in the station, armed and declaring martial law. You Bolu, the chief of the Fifth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, upon hearing the news, immediately dispatched Inspector Li with armed police officers to investigate the scene. However, the assailants had already fled and disappeared without a trace. Later, police officer Chen Changmin found two rows of bullets on the ground in front of the station and took them to the district for record. The district chief immediately went to the Public Security Bureau to report the incident to Director Chen Xizeng.

▲ Song's Interview: Afterwards, Finance Minister Song Ziwen issued a statement saying, "I arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing on the overnight express train, arriving at the station at 7:00 AM this morning. After getting off the train, I walked to a point about fifteen feet from the station door when I suddenly heard gunshots coming from both sides. I knew that someone was trying to assassinate me. I took off the white hat I was wearing and threw it into a dark corner of the station to avoid being conspicuous, and I mingled with the crowd, hiding behind a pillar. I also drew my handgun for self-defense. As soon as I reached the pillar, I heard the sound of an exploding bomb, two loud bangs. Smoke filled the station, and bullets flew in all directions. My guards also returned fire. The shooting lasted for about five minutes before it stopped. By this time, everyone except my party had fled the station. According to what my guards saw, at least four assailants were firing guns, or perhaps more than that. When the smoke cleared, I saw that my secretary, Mr. Tang Yuluo, had fallen, shot. Tang was walking shoulder to shoulder with me when the assailants opened fire. He was hit in the bladder, hip, and arm. The bullets came from both sides. There were bullet holes in his hat and briefcase. I am taller than him and escaped without any injury, which is truly unbelievable. Mr. Tang has died from his injuries. Two of my guards were also injured, one seriously. Passengers were also injured. I have received repeated warnings that people in Guangzhou were plotting against me, but I did not expect them to take such an extreme measure as to attempt assassination."

▲ Guard's Interview: In Finance Minister Song's statement, he said that two of his guards were injured, one seriously, but after inquiring with various parties, it was said that only one guard was injured. Our newspaper reporter interviewed the injured guard, Min Ziqing, at Baolong Hospital last night. The shrapnel from Min's right leg had not yet been removed. He was in good spirits. According to him, only one of the six guards was injured. The situation at the time was extremely dangerous. There were about six or seven assailants in sight, all young men wearing white long gowns. At first, they fired handguns, and then they used hand grenades. We had two portable machine guns and four new-style rifles, but we used the new-style rifles this morning because we were afraid that the portable machine guns would injure innocent people. The entire hall was filled with smoke, and we lost our target, allowing the assailants to escape, which is regrettable.

▲ Secretary Wang's Interview: Wang Shiduo, a secretary of the Control Yuan who was recovering from his injuries at Fumin Hospital yesterday, told the reporter, "I came to Shanghai on the night train. After arriving at the North Station this morning (i.e., yesterday morning), I got off the train and exited the station. As I walked to the gate of the information desk, there was a sudden loud noise. Then, bullets came from all directions, front, back, left, and right. The sound of gunfire filled my ears. I quickly lay down on the ground to avoid the bullets. At that time, I was disoriented, so I could not recognize what was happening around me, nor the faces and clothing of the assailants. I did not even feel the pain of the shrapnel wound to my right foot. After the incident, I only knew that my right foot was bleeding and injured. So I exited the station, hired a car, and went to Fumin Hospital for treatment."

▲ Director Chen's Interview: A reporter from the "New Voice News Agency" made a special trip to interview Chen Xizeng, the director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, to clarify the truth of the matter and asked for information. Director Chen said, "I received the alarm at 7:30 AM this morning and first went to Minister Song's residence to inquire. Upon meeting Minister Song, I saw that he was safe and sound, and I was relieved. According to eyewitnesses at the scene, the perpetrators were mostly wearing white clothes and speaking Cantonese. From this, it seems that it was done by Cantonese reactionaries. As for the reasons, they are not yet fully understood. I have strictly ordered my subordinates to secretly investigate. However, the police authority within the railway bureau's boundaries has always been the responsibility of the railway police. Therefore, the south side of the iron shed door outside the two-railway station is the concession, and the inside of the iron shed is entirely controlled by the railway police. The Municipal Public Security Bureau police are far away at the Baoshan Road intersection. The only person dispatched to the station is one person who is responsible for inspecting luggage for contraband, who works with the investigation team of the Garrison Headquarters. Except in special circumstances, the Municipal Public Security Bureau police are not allowed to go to the station entrance without permission. In this incident, if it were not for the efforts of Minister Song's guards, the consequences would have been unimaginable. However, Nanjing and Shanghai are close, and important officials of the National Government travel back and forth frequently. The Bureau is restricted by its authority and precedents, so it is difficult to fully fulfill its responsibilities, which is regrettable. I sincerely hope that the Ministry of Railways will learn from the past and make changes in the future, so that the police of the Bureau can cooperate with the railway police. This would prevent unexpected dangers from happening again and would be more convenient in other matters, such as checking car licenses and arresting criminals. Within the station, it is often difficult to get the railway police to fully assist. It is necessary to formally notify them in advance before execution, which is like dealing with the concession police station. The division of authority is fragmented, which is very strange."

▲ Condolences to Mr. Song: After the incident occurred, important figures in Shanghai, such as Mayor Zhang Qun, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Haian, and important figures in the banking industry, visited Mr. Song's residence to offer their condolences. Mr. Song rested at his residence in the morning. At around 5:00 PM in the afternoon, he went to Kong Xiangxi's residence to visit Mrs. Kong.

▲ Inspection of the North Station: After the incident occurred yesterday morning, at around 8:00 AM, the Longhua Garrison Headquarters dispatched a platoon of soldiers to the station to provide protection. The Public Security Bureau also sent armed police officers to maintain order, creating a tense atmosphere. The reporter went to the North Station to inspect at around 10:00 AM in the morning and saw more than a dozen bullet holes in the ceiling of the hall. There were also several bullet holes in the wall and glass windows of the inspection office. There was a large bullet hole in the lower part of the cement column on the right side. Station staff members who were present yesterday morning were all frightened, which showed the intensity of the fierce battle at the time.

▲ One Suspect: After the incident, the Public Concession Police Department dispatched detectives to arrest the assailants. They soon apprehended one suspect in the Anle Hotel on North Zhejiang Road.

Page 14

It is said that his surname is, given name Dan, from, 23 years old. He went to the Anle Hotel at about 6:00 AM, and went out half an hour later, saying he was going to eat. He returned at about 7:30 AM. It is also said that he came to Shanghai on the same train as Mr. Song and previously studied at the Central Military Academy in Nanjing. Because there are suspicions, the concession handed him over to the Chinese authorities for interrogation.

Yesterday, the City Mourned Compatriots in a Bitter Wind and Rain

▲ Business and Industry Closed for Half a Day

▲ Committee Members Take Oath of Office

The Shanghai Municipal All-Circles Memorial Service for the Deceased Overseas Chinese in Korea and the Re-swearing Ceremony of the Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association Committee Members were held together at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 AM yesterday. More than 2,000 people from all walks of life attended the meeting, including Wang Laixiao, Wang Yansong, Yuan Ludeng, Ye Huijun, Xi Yushu, Wang Jian, Feng Yixian, Cai Guo Jingluan, Guo Jinglun, Zheng Chengqing, Yan Esheng, Lu Xingzhuang, Hou Dachun, Li Yongxiang, and representatives from all walks of life. The entire city closed for half a day in the morning and lowered flags for one day to mourn. The meeting and business closure are recorded separately below.

▲ Citywide Closure: Yesterday, in mourning for the deceased overseas Chinese in Korea, all sectors in Shanghai lowered flags to half-mast and closed for half a day in the morning. Almost all businesses on Nanjing Road, Henan Road, Jiangxi Road, etc., were closed, with very few remaining partially open. Bookstores such as Commercial Press, China Book Company, World Book Company, and Datong Book Company; department stores such as Sincere, Wing On, Sun Sun, and Lihua; and various banks, money shops, and exchanges were all completely closed in the morning.

Photography of all sectors in Shanghai Memorial Service for Deceased Overseas Chinese in Korea (Photo by This Newspaper)

The Spirit Remains - The Soul Returns

This, coupled with the cloudy skies and continuous heavy rain, seemed as if the heavens themselves could not bear the grief and indignation. It was not until after 12:00 PM that businesses reopened uniformly. In the Chinese areas, the major stores on Zhonghua Road and Minguo Road also lowered flags to half-mast and closed in the morning. The lowering of flags on the main roads was quite consistent, and it did not stop due to the heavy rain.

▲ Venue Arrangement: The Party and National flags were hung at the entrance, with a bamboo and cloth horizontal plaque reading "Shanghai Municipal All-Circles Memorial Service for the Deceased Overseas Chinese in Korea" placed horizontally. At the entrance of the venue, there was a mourning couplet from the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department: "Dying at home is not as good as dying for the country," "Catching the thief is not as good as catching the king." The venue was filled with mourning couplets and scrolls sent by all sectors. In the memorial hall, the spirit tablets of the deceased overseas Chinese in Korea were enshrined, surrounded by many wreaths. Mourning couplets from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce were hung on both sides. The entire venue was white, extremely desolate.

▲ Participating Organizations: The organizations that participated yesterday included the First, Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth, Sixth, Seventh, Eighth, and Ninth District Party Departments, as well as their branches; various district education associations; agricultural associations; publishing industry guilds; cigarette industry guilds; lithographic industry guilds; knitting industry guilds; shipbuilding industry guilds; water and electricity industry guilds; newspaper delivery industry guilds; transportation industry guilds; coal industry guilds; cotton fabric industry guilds; military uniform industry guilds; tobacco industry guilds; Korean community associations; National Goods Preservation Association; women's associations; and more than 300 other organizations, with more than 2,000 representatives.

▲ Conference Officials: The presidium consisted of Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Hou Dachun, Yu Qiaqing, Tao Baichuan, Lu Jingshi, and Chen Tingrui. The chief celebrant was Ye Huijun, the master of ceremonies was Zheng Chengqing, the recorder was Xue Guangqian, and the receptionists were Yuan Hongjun, Li Zhang, Chen Quyun, and Zhang Honghai.

▲ Conference Order: 1. All stand at attention; 2. Presidium takes their seats; 3. Chief celebrant takes office (Ye Huijun); 4. Play mournful music; 5. Sing the Party anthem; 6. Bow three times to the Party and National flags and the portrait of the Prime Minister; 7. Chairman respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will (Wang Tingsong); 8. Silent tribute for three minutes to mourn the deceased overseas Chinese in Korea; 9. Respectfully present wreaths; 10. Respectfully read the memorial text (Wang Xiaolai); 11. Committee members of the Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association take the oath of office; 12. Chairman's report (Wang Xiaolai); 13. Representatives of various agencies deliver speeches; 14. Representatives from all walks of life give speeches; 15. Shout slogans; 16. Play mournful music; 17. Adjourn the meeting.

▲ Chairman's Report: After the ceremony was performed as scheduled, Wang Xiaolai was nominated by the presidium to give a report, briefly stating: "Today we are holding this conference to mourn the deceased overseas Chinese, and all industries in the city have stopped business for half a day and uniformly lowered flags to half-mast to express our grief. This shows that the national spirit of our country is no longer what it used to be. Today's meeting is held on the one hand to commemorate the overseas Chinese, and on the other hand to hold the re-swearing ceremony for the committee members of the Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association. Recalling the wanton brutality of the Japanese this time can be called an unprecedented catastrophe for Chinese overseas Chinese. If the people of the whole country do not rise up to help with such a tragedy, the international status will inevitably decline further. Now the Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association has been formally established, and all anti-Japanese measures are being planned and implemented in detail. I hope that the people will work together and cooperate with the Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association to move forward, and there will be satisfactory results in the future. This is the responsibility of those who survive. The occurrence of this incident was tragic, and heaven and earth wept. It is indeed a crisis for the Chinese nation to strive for its own survival."

▲ Third Conference Memorial Text: On July 23rd, the 20th year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Committee respectfully offers a sacrifice of modest wine and pure food to the spirits of the deceased overseas Chinese in Korea, saying: Alas, without diligent effort, how can people live and rest in peace? Seeking a livelihood in foreign lands is like floating duckweed, rootless and drifting, left to the mercy of others, like a knife and cutting board. Korea, the three Hans, is the same vein as our divine land. People of the same race have interacted for centuries. People of Lu crossed the sea to the east, like water returning to a valley, each receiving a share, forming villages of their own. Fraud and deception were dispelled, and they lived in peace, farming and cultivating. But misfortune arrived, and Japan grew violent. Thieves hated their masters, bullying the weak with the strong, employing tiger cubs and stirring up locusts, invading and plundering. In the shadows of Pyongyang, in the outskirts of Seoul, they cut down trees and raised poles, conducting a great search for ten days. Alas, our overseas Chinese, their strength restricted, like overturned nests with no intact eggs, like frost falling on duckweed. Merchants lost their assets, farmers lost their harvests. Escaping from the jaws of tigers, they were satiated with the edge of swords. Six thousand gentlemen, reduced to insects and monkeys. Who will avenge the national shame? Who will act as a shepherd? May your spirits be aware, accept this one drink. Enjoy the sacrifice.

▲ Committee Oath: After the chairman recited the memorial text, all the committee members of the Anti-Japanese and Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association took their re-oath of office. The oath read: "We swear in all sincerity that under the leadership of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department of the Chinese Kuomintang, we will strive to work against Japan and aid overseas Chinese. We will not be self-serving, we will not engage in corruption, we will work diligently, and we will use people with caution. If we violate this oath, we are willing to accept the most severe punishment. We solemnly swear."

▲ Representative's Speech: Huang Zhaoxiong, the representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a speech, briefly stating: "This time, the Japanese instigated the Korean people to massacre overseas Chinese, and all Chinese people are filled with righteous indignation. Today's memorial service should recognize that this Japanese action against China is a systematic and planned implementation of the policy of invading and occupying Manchuria and Mongolia. The affected overseas Chinese are now suffering death and injury. I hope that the people of the country will unite to help the overseas Chinese, use the entire strength of the people to engage in the relief movement, and, on the one hand, unite as a whole to be the government's backing in diplomatic relations with Japan. Then the future of the nation will probably have hope.

▲ Speeches from All Sectors: The representative of the Korean United Association gave a speech, briefly stating: "This time, the Japanese instigated the Korean people to massacre overseas Chinese, and I would like to express my apologies on behalf of all the Korean people. However, the occurrence of this tragedy was not the intention of the Korean people themselves. Because Korea is a conquered country, a colony, not comparable to other independent countries. Under the iron heel of Japanese imperialism, there is no freedom of action to speak of. It was entirely the Japanese who used bad elements of the Korean people to massacre overseas Chinese. Please, nationals of your esteemed country, be understanding and please support the Korean people's liberation movement. Next, Cai Guo Jingluan, Liu Zhongda, the representative of the Incheon Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Korea, Lin Kecong, the representative of the Women's Association, and Zhu Xuefan, the representative of the workers, gave very painful speeches (details omitted). Finally, Tao Baichuan, nominated by the presidium, gave a closing speech and adjourned the meeting.

▲ Conference Slogans: (1) To mourn the deceased overseas Chinese, we must strive for the anti-Japanese movement; (2) To mourn the deceased overseas Chinese, we must strictly implement economic severance; (3) All compatriots, unite to avenge the deceased overseas Chinese; (4) All compatriots across the country, unite and permanently sever economic ties with Japan; (5) All compatriots across the country, unite and overthrow Japanese imperialism; (6) The spirit of the deceased overseas Chinese will never die!

Boycott of Japanese Goods Begins Yesterday with Registration

▲ Announcement of Regulations for Registering Japanese Goods

▲ Recommendation of Yu Qiaqing as Director of External Affairs

The various circles' Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee, during yesterday morning's memorial service, after the committee members took their oaths of office, officially began registering Japanese goods at 1:00 PM. The registration was overseen by the head of the registration section, Chen Tingrui, and Xi Yushu. At 2:00 PM, the committee held its second committee meeting. Details of each are recorded below.

▲ Registration Begins The Registration Section of the Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee officially began registering Japanese goods yesterday afternoon. Those who came to register included Xin Ri Feng Foreign Sundries Store, Tongde Dye Factory, Yonghe Dye Factory, Henry Soap and Candle Factory, Xie Feng Heng Yarn Store, Heng Ji Sundries Store, Heng Cheng Tai Lumber Store, Heng Xing Lumber Store, Yongcheng Cloth Factory, Wiener Trading Company, Shi Xin Bookstore, Da Sheng Bookstore, Da Shanghai Rubber Factory, Nanshi Yongkangxiang Electrical Supplies Store, Dahe Dye Factory, Wenhua Bookstore, Wan Mao Chang Cotton Cloth Store, Dingxin Dyeing and Weaving Factory, and the Shanghai Branch of Hua Feng Industrial Raw Materials Company.

▲ Registration Regulations The Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee issued Public Notice No. 6 yesterday, outlining the regulations for registering Japanese goods: (1) Each business should first obtain three registration forms from the Registration Section of this Committee; (2) After obtaining the registration forms, each item should be filled out in detail on all three forms without any omissions; (3) If there is anything unclear on the forms, please inquire at the Registration Section for clarification to avoid errors; (4) The handwriting on the forms must be clear and legible; (5) After the forms are completed, they must be signed and sealed by the manager of the business to show seriousness; (6) If the forms are not sufficient, more can be obtained from the Registration Section of this Committee; (7) The "Label Preparation" section of the forms should be left blank and filled in by the Registration Section of this Committee.

▲ Committee Meeting At 2:00 PM, the second committee meeting continued. Committee members present were Wang Xiaolai, Yan E'sheng, Lu Jingshi, Wang Yansong, Chen Songyuan, Cheng Zhusun, Wang Hanliang, Chen Peide, Wang Jiean, Feng Yixian, Hou Dachun, Lin Kecong, Lu Xingzhuang, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yichen, Zheng Chengqing, Li Cishan, Li Wenjie, Chen Ya'fu, Zhang Huijun, Liu Shimu, Wang Zhuping, Li Yongxiang, Wang Wenhua, Zhou Xuexiang and twenty-five others. Wang Xiaolai was elected as chairman and Xue Guangqian as recorder. The following motions were discussed: (1) Discussion of the Committee's constitution. Resolution: Passed; (2) Discussion of the Committee's finances. Resolution: Wang Yansong, Tao Baichuan, and Hou Dachun were recommended to borrow 50,000 yuan from the Municipal Party Headquarters; (3) Discussion of adding design committee members. Resolution: Lu Xingzhuang, Feng Yixian, and Li Wenjie were added as members of the Design Committee. The convener of the Design Committee, Chen Songyuan, was also tasked with finding two individuals each from the sugar, seafood, coal, and paper industries to serve as design committee members; (4) Discussion of the candidate for Director of the External Affairs Section. Resolution: Standing Committee member Yu Qiaqing was recommended to concurrently serve as Director of the External Affairs Section; (5) Discussion of reward and punishment regulations. Resolution: Referred to the Standing Committee for review; (6) Discussion of the handling of confiscated Japanese goods. Resolution: To be handled jointly by the Inspection, Investigation, and Storage Sections; (7) Discussion of the date for the next Executive Committee meeting. Resolution: Scheduled for 4:00 PM next Monday.

▲ Committee Constitution The full text of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee constitution passed yesterday is as follows: Article 1: This Committee is established and organized by the Shanghai Municipal All-Circles Representative Assembly. Article 2: The scope of this Committee's work is to oppose Japan and aid compatriots. It is named the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee. Article 3: The Committee's address is located at the Former Tianhou Palace on North Henan Road in Shanghai. Article 4: This Committee has thirty-seven executive committee members, elected by the Shanghai Municipal All-Circles Representative Assembly. Article 5: This Committee has seven standing committee members, elected by ballot from among the executive committee members. Article 6: This Committee has one secretary-general and two secretaries, with candidates nominated by the standing committee members and decided by the executive committee. Article 7: This Committee is divided into seven sections: (1) General Affairs, (2) Publicity, (3) Inspection, (4) Investigation, (5) Registration, (6) Storage, (7) External Affairs. Each section has a director and deputy director. Article 8: The director and deputy director of each section are recommended by the executive committee members. Article 9: Each section may, depending on the complexity of its affairs, divide its work into divisions and establish staff members. The division of work and the number of staff members are determined by the director of each section, submitted to the standing committee for decision and reported to the committee. Article 10: This Committee may establish various specialized committees as necessary in practice, and their rules will be determined separately. Article 11: The daily affairs of this Committee are handled with the consent and signature of four standing committee members. Article 12: Regular withdrawals from this Committee must be signed by four or more standing committee members to be valid. Article 13: Meetings of the Executive Committee of this Committee are held every Wednesday at 5:00 PM. Article 14: Meetings of the Standing Committee of this Committee are held every Tuesday and Friday at 1:00 PM. Article 15: Special meetings of the entire committee and standing committee may be convened when necessary. Article 16: During meetings, one standing committee member is elected as chairman, and resolutions are passed with the attendance of more than half of the committee members and the consent of more than half of those present. Article 17: The detailed rules of this Committee will be determined separately. Article 18: This constitution will be submitted to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters for approval and record after being passed by the Executive Committee, and the same applies to any amendments.

Confiscation of Japanese Goods Continues

▲ Transportation Industry Announces Suspension of Transport

Since the Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee resolved that all Japanese goods are not allowed to be moved and began inspection work on one hand, Japanese goods being transported for export have been seized at any time. As a result, the transportation industry decided yesterday to notify all colleagues to suspend the collection of Japanese goods from today (the 24th). The news yesterday is recorded as follows:

▲ Continued Confiscation The Committee received a tip the day before yesterday that a large batch of Japanese goods was about to be smuggled to Hangzhou on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line at the South Station. The Inspection Section of the Committee immediately sent personnel to confiscate them. The details were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now reported that the number of Japanese goods is actually more than 1,100 tons. Except for 400 tons that had already been loaded onto the train when the Anti-Japanese Committee sent personnel to seal them off and could not be stopped, the remaining 700 tons were all confiscated at the station. More than a dozen officials from the Inspection Section of the Committee guarded the station overnight in the rain. Yesterday, the Railway Bureau temporarily handed over the goods to the railway warehouse for safekeeping, pending a resolution by the Anti-Japanese Committee. Also, at 5:00 PM yesterday, a large batch of Japanese goods at the North Station was trying to be shipped out and was discovered and confiscated by the Committee. It is reported that the Committee has also rented a patrol boat for the transportation of Japanese goods in the middle waterway of the Huangpu River to closely patrol and prevent any escape.

▲ Suspension of Japanese Goods Transportation The Shanghai Transportation Industry Association issued a notice yesterday, saying: "For the matter of the notice, we have received a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on the four measures for the disposal of Japanese goods decided by the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Compatriots Committee, hoping that everyone will pay attention, etc." According to the industry, it is acting as an agent for the transportation of goods, and there is no distinction between accepting customer goods. During this anti-Japanese wave, before the announcement, Japanese goods that have been received, or that are still stored in the railway warehouse due to lack of vehicles, or that have already been transported to the middle of the journey and have not yet arrived at the destination, are inevitable. It is quite difficult to conduct a detailed investigation for a while, and it is deeply feared that it will be implicated for no reason. Therefore, the company convened an emergency meeting of all colleagues in the city today and decided on four measures as follows: (A) The Japanese goods that have been received but have not yet been transported will be checked in detail by the end of today and reported to the association. The association will compile a detailed list and report it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for registration. (B) From today (ie, the 24th), the collection of Japanese goods will be suspended, and a notice will be posted at the cargo warehouses at both Maigen Road and the North Station to make it known to everyone. (C) The association will issue a wooden stamp with the words "Jointly agreed by the industry, if there are any Japanese goods or disguised goods in the consigned goods, once discovered, the cargo owner will be responsible, and the carrier will not be involved," etc., and distribute them to the industry for universal use. (D) For those that have been transported out but have not yet reached the destination, or have just arrived but have not yet been unloaded, the local industry should report to the association for registration nearby. In addition to notifying the industry to comply with it, it is a special notice for the attention of all circles.

Shanghai Lawyers' Association Executive and Supervisory Committee Resolves Three Lawyers' Withdrawal Cases

▲ Zheng Yuxiu's Withdrawal Referred for Disciplinary Action

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association convened its 84th joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees at 6:00 PM yesterday. Committee members present were Zhao Zuwei, Lu Shaozong, Liu Zuwang, Lu Jianai, Cai Nipei, Zhang Feixiong, Tang Yingsong, Tan Yigong, Yu Zhongluo, Li Shirui, Wen Chao, Shen Junru, etc. Lu Shaozong chaired the meeting and Dai Jixian recorded the minutes. The proposals are recorded below: (1) Member Ren Zhennan expressed disagreement with the resolution to withdraw from the association and requested reconsideration. (Resolution) Reply to the member that the association believes that Member Ren has violated the Lawyers' Association Charter and Regulations. If he disagrees, he can handle it in accordance with Article 34 of the Lawyers' Association Charter. (2) The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau sent letters inquiring about lawyer Yan Luqing's voluntary registration on behalf of creditors of the Riye Bank and the issuance of 10% of the deposits by the Riye Bank Liquidation Office, which was abusively issued at a discount of 85%, which is tantamount to fraud. (Resolution) Recommend Committee members Tang Yingsong and Zhang Feixiong to review and report before further verification. (3) Luo Buzhou sent a letter reporting that lawyer Zheng Yuxiu had returned the public fee of 1,000 yuan and requested to withdraw the previous letter. (Resolution) Not to be withdrawn. (4) Chen Zemin, Lu Jianai, and Liu Zuwang, the third committee member, investigated the details of the witnesses and evidence of lawyer Zheng Yuwei's acceptance of public fees and dereliction of duty. The investigation report is recorded. (Recorded later) The committee members present expressed their opinions. The chairman summarized the opinions and proposed two measures: (A) Refer for disciplinary action. (B) Report the withdrawal from the association and refer for disciplinary action. Please vote. As a result, the majority passed the second measure to report to the superior court on member Zheng Yuxiu's withdrawal and request the court to refer for disciplinary action. (5) Members Ni, etc. sent a letter requesting reconsideration of member Jiang Shiyi's violation of the association rules. (Resolution) Reply to the members that if they disagree with the resolution of this meeting, they can handle it in accordance with Article 34 of the Lawyers' Association Charter. (6) Lawyers Yao Jianguang, Ke Tingzhen, Chen Feng, and Ma Hongyuan applied for membership. (Resolution) Passed. The report of the three committee members Chen Zemin, Lu Jianai, and Liu Zuwang is recorded later: For the matter of the report, on the 12th of this month, this association was recommended to quickly investigate and report on the case of Luo Buzhou's letter to lawyer Zheng Yuxiu's dereliction of duty, etc. Upon receiving this, Zemin and others immediately went to Luo Buzhou's office to inquire. Luo went to the capital for business and could not be met. They went to the witness Li Shirui's office for detailed investigation. Lawyer Li handed over the evidence for review: (1) The receipt for public fees issued by Zheng Yuxiu, with Mr. Li Cishan's name on it. (2) A delivery book with the stamp of Zheng Yuxiu's law firm on September 14th and 13th. (3) Two stubs of checks from Tongyi Trust Company. (4) Two drafts of letters requesting the return of public fees. All of the above have probative value in this case. The inquiries are recorded in detail. They also went to Tongyi Company to find out that the checks delivered by Lawyer Li for public fees were all filled in with the words "Lawyer Zheng Yuxiu" and collected by Hongsheng Qianzhuang. This was the investigation before the 19th. When the meeting was held on the 19th, another letter from Zheng Yuxiu was handed down, ordering a quick investigation and report. Therefore, on the 20th, they went to Luo Buzhou's office to meet Tan Yiqie. According to Tan, all the evidence was at Lawyer Li's office. However, he stated that he had made an appointment with Lawyer Li at Lawyer Zheng's office in October of the previous year. He had gone alone once a few days later. He had gone twice in March of last year. Lawyer Zheng was not in the office, so he had not met him. The details are also recorded in the minutes. Lawyer Wu Chengyu visited many times and did not meet him. He only spoke to Zemin once on the phone. According to him, he did not know that Lawyer Zheng was involved in the case. On the 21st, they visited Lawyer Zheng and did not meet him. Lawyer Zheng called in the morning and made an appointment. They went in the afternoon. According to Zheng, he had explained to Lawyer Li that he would not appear in court. Luo Buzhou had never been there since making the appointment. Zemin and others asked to see the entrustment contract, but he said that there was no case file, so it was not clear whether there was a contract. Moreover, the office had moved several times, so it was difficult to find it. The rest is also recorded in detail in the minutes. The three investigation records, along with the three pieces of evidence, are submitted for reference. It is also stated that the delivery book under the evidence item is needed for daily use, so it was not handed over to the meeting. This report is respectfully submitted. Investigators of the Executive and Supervisory Committee: Chen Zemin, Lu Jianai, Liu Zuwang. 20.7.13.

Local News Two

Two Thousand Yuan in Campaign Funds for a Detective Squad Leader

▲ Turns Out It Was a Big Scam

▲ Dared to Pay at the Public Security Bureau

Zhang Guobin, a local, 38 years old, used to be in the coal business and is now unemployed. On the 1st of this month, he came to Shanghai from Hangzhou to look for a job. That night, he went to the rooftop garden of the New World Company and met an old friend, Zhang Zheng from Hunan. After talking, he learned that Guobin was unemployed, so he offered to introduce him to a job, arranging to meet again at the Qinglian Pavilion teahouse at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Hubei Road the next day. On the 2nd, Guobin and Zhang Zheng met at the Qinglian Pavilion. Zhang Zheng said that he was friendly with senior officials of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and was willing to help him find the position of captain of the First Detective Squad, arranging to meet again on the 4th. After speaking, they dispersed. On the 4th, Guobin and Zhang Zheng met at the Qinglian Pavilion again. Zhang Zheng said that he had already arranged it, but he needed

▲ Two Thousand Yuan in Funds as campaign funds. Guobin, eager to find a job, did not distinguish between truth and falsehood and rashly agreed. He then asked his younger brother, Zhang Tongbang, to raise 1,000 yuan in cash and went with Zhang Zheng to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to pay. When they reached the entrance of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Zhang Zheng instructed Guobin to wait at the entrance and ordered him to hand over 1,000 yuan and his resume to him inside. After a while, Zhang came out and said that he had contacted Section Chief Wang of the Third Section.

▲ Sent Campaign Funds He only needed to wait quietly for the appointment. The letter of appointment would be issued around the 7th or 8th, and another 1,000 yuan would be paid at that time. Guobin then went to the Shenzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road on the 8th and opened room 421 to wait for the appointment. On the 11th, Zhang Zheng came as expected and took out No. 1715,

▲ A Letter of Appointment with the seals of Municipal Public Security Bureau Director Chen, Squad Leader Lu, and Section Chief Wang was handed over to Guobin, and Guobin also handed over the remaining 1,000 yuan in cash to Zhang. After receiving the money, Zhang also said that if he wanted to carry out his duties and arrest criminals, he would need to provide another certificate, which would be given in a few days. After speaking, he took the money and left. After a few days, Guobin became suspicious because he disappeared without a trace. He then asked his younger brother, Zhang Tongbang, to take the letter of appointment to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to inquire. After Director Chen examined it,

▲ Learned It Was Forged and ordered an investigation. Guobin then reported to the Patrol Room. Until 7:00 PM the night before last, Zhang Zheng went to Shenzhou to visit Guobin and was secretly reported to the Old Gate Patrol Room, which sent detective Yan Yu to arrest Zhang Zheng and detain him in the Patrol Room. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Special District Court. According to Patrol Room lawyer Ru Bao Yi, who detailed the above situation, the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent personnel to the case today, requesting a transfer. However, according to my lawyer's opinion, the most important thing is to first study the defendant,

▲ The Location of the Crime Where is it? If it is in the Concession, the Municipal Council should prosecute according to law. Then Zhang Guobin and witness Zhang Tongbang surrendered, proving everything. When questioned, the defendant confessed, "I entrusted this matter to my friend Wang Chundai to handle. Wang claimed to be working in the Municipal Government. All the letters of appointment were also given to me by Wang, but I did not receive the money." According to the public security detectives who delivered the official documents, they said that they were ordered by the director because the money was delivered at the Public Security Bureau.

▲ There May Be Other Circumstances so they requested a transfer. Judge Xu Jiashi declared after checking the report, "After examining the circumstances of this case, the location of the crime is in both the Chinese and Concession areas. This court and the local court can both accept the case, so the court that accepted the case first should handle it." Patrol Room lawyer Ru then declared in court that he was prosecuting under Article 225 of the Criminal Law. Judge Xu then ordered a postponement of two weeks. Zhang Zheng was allowed to be taken to the Public Security Bureau for investigation and then sent back for trial.

Prison Inmates on Hunger Strike

▲ Western Woman Mrs. Van der Cruysen

The Great America Evening Post said that a Western woman began a hunger strike in the Xiamen Road Western Prison this morning (the 23rd). The woman is Mrs. Van der Cruysen, a communist propaganda criminal arrested by the Public Concession Patrol Room a few weeks ago. After she and her husband were sent to the Special District Court, they were detained pending further trial. According to General Patrolman Martin, Mrs. Van has been threatening to go on a hunger strike for several days and began refusing breakfast this morning. However, the prison staff is not worried about this. If Mrs. Van really refuses to eat, the prison doctor will be called to handle it according to the usual procedures. Hunger strikes in the Public Concession Western Prison are common, but it is the first time that it has been done by Western women.

Director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Visits the Shanghai-South China and French Water Plants

▲ Expresses Satisfaction and Approval

Huang Boqiao, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, accompanied by Sun Guangyi, a technician from the Bureau, and Li Qingquan, a technician, went to the inland water plant the day before yesterday to inspect the plant's newly built rapid filter pool, clear water pool, and electrical inlet machine room, and electrical outlet machine room, and other new projects, which have all been completed. All the old-fashioned steam water pump machines have been abandoned and replaced with electric water pump machines, so the water volume is unusually abundant and the water pressure has increased several times. In terms of water quality, it has also made considerable progress compared to the past due to sand filtration and three times of green gas disinfection. After being led around by Yao Mulian, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the company, Lu Bohong, Director, Dong Engineer, and Lu, Chief of the General Affairs Section, they felt very satisfied. They then rushed to the Machine Factory Street to visit the French Water Plant, where Mr. Meng Suo, the French General Manager, personally led them. Each part from the inlet to the outlet was explained in detail. The water inlet of the plant uses a water absorption trumpet, which can automatically rise and fall with the tide, and has not experienced any failures since it started generating electricity itself in April of this year. Therefore, Huang expressed his appreciation for the plant's equipment and management.

Astronomer Ye Youqin predicted that the heavy thunderstorms in Shanghai on the morning of July 6th and the major earthquake in Ecuador, South America on the morning of the 17th were both closely related to the date table of earthquake storms predicted by Yu in the Shenbao on January 1st of this year. Now it is predicted again that there will be wind, rain, and high tides in Shanghai on August 14th and 15th and September 12th and 13th. This summer is a cold and rainy year, and its temperature cannot be higher than 96 degrees Fahrenheit. The inland is rainy and Shanghai is cold, which is caused by the extreme heat in the Americas.

Bandit Chief Lin Meisheng of Fujian Province Arrested

Lin Meisheng, a well-known bandit in Fujian who had not been captured for several years, is over thirty years old, tall and strong, with piercing eyes and a fierce light shining like electricity. When he was in Fuzhou and other places, he killed and set fires almost every day. Now, the local authorities are sending detectives out day and night to visit and arrest him. Lin then sneaked into Shanghai, first staying in the Public Concession. On the day of his arrest, he suddenly rented a room at No. 3 Anle Palace Hotel on Aiduya Road. Deng Jingming, the chief of the detective team of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, learned of Lin's whereabouts. At the same time, an official from Fujian came to report that the bandit was hiding in the Public Concession and asked for assistance. Therefore, he immediately dispatched officers Yang Fengqi, Xu Pengfei, Wang Bin, etc., on the 21st, together with the patrol room detectives, to rush to Anle Palace Hotel in the French Concession, where the bandit Lin was last hiding, and captured him. However, since Lin was fierce and brave, he was unwilling to be captured without a fight. Moreover, the captors were in a hotel and it was inconvenient to draw guns and open fire, hurting tourists. Therefore, the two sides fought hand-to-hand, and the situation was extremely fierce. However, in the end, due to the disparity in strength, Lin surrendered when he was exhausted. It is reported that he was taken back by the detective team for questioning on the afternoon of the 22nd.

Shanghai Pudong Fellow Villagers Association Initiated

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Relieves the Water Shortage in Chongdeli, Zhabei

▲ Urging the Addition of Public Faucets

There are more than 20 bungalows opposite Chongdeli on Nantong Road, Zhabei, with only one public tap installed. During this hot summer, the demand for water is urgent and insufficient, resulting in frequent disputes among residents. Moreover, the tap is set up on the side of the road, and anyone can take it at will, so there are even more disputes. After the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities received a report from the residents there, it sent personnel to investigate and confirmed that it was true. The Great America Evening Post said that Hill, the American expert hired by the Municipal Council to investigate the Water Company, is now scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the Japanese Queen ship on September 1st. A Famous Beach Opera Star, Shi Xiangyun, Stage a Home Theft

▲ Two Women Suffer Unjust Accusations

A certain Mrs. Yong, residing near Xiaobeimen, set up a steamed rice stall daily at the entrance of a rice shop south of the Ningfeng Inn on Min'an Road. This spring, a fellow villager, surnamed Fei, entrusted her with the care of a foster son, providing a monthly allowance of six yuan for nursing. During business hours, she always brought the child, who sat on a mat beside her. A woman selling cakes at a nearby stall also cherished the child, often holding and playing with him, which became customary. Unexpectedly, on the third day of the fifth lunar month, while Mrs. Yong was selling rice, the child sitting on the mat beside her suddenly disappeared. Suspecting the cake-selling woman of conspiring to abduct the child, they engaged in heated arguments, but the doubts remained unresolved. When the foster parent learned of this, he sent out scouts everywhere, but to no avail. He then beat a gong and searched along the streets and alleys for several days, but it was like searching for a yellow crane – impossible. Unable to do otherwise, he reported to the police station, even having both Mrs. Yong and the cake-selling woman arrested on suspicion of conspiracy to abduct the child. More than a month passed, and the injustice remained unaddressed. It wasn't until the afternoon of the 21st of this month, at three o'clock, that someone discovered the child at the home of Shi Xiangyun, a famous beach opera singer, in the third lane of the Mintiniyin Road. The foster parent reported this to the Songshan Road Police Station, which immediately dispatched detectives to Shi's home. They found a six-month-old boy under the stairs. It was said that the child had been secretly taken by Shi Xiangyun's female apprentice. Now, Shi's father, Liansheng, has hired a wet nurse to care for the child at home. The unjust case has finally come to light.

Chief Clerk Accused of Seducing an Underage Girl

Sun Fusheng, a Suzhou native, age 41, working as a chief clerk at the residence of a certain Westerner at No. 1490 Xiafei Road in the French Concession, has recently engaged lawyer Chen Bingxing to file a lawsuit with the Special District Court, accusing Yang Genquan of No. 244 Xinzha Road and Qian Asan, a chief clerk working for a Westerner in Room 3, No. 181 Maitini Road in the French Concession, of obstructing marriage and other offenses. The essence of his lawsuit is as follows:

For seducing an ignorant girl and eloping with her privately, and for filing an incidental private prosecution. My own daughter, Fengdi, is currently 19 years old and studies at Tongyi Public School. She is honest and chaste. In order to avoid a desolate old age, I adopted a son early on, hoping he would marry into the family and provide support. However, the first defendant, Yang Genquan, a married man, saw that Fengdi was slightly attractive and had been coveting her for a long time, attempting to seduce her in every possible way. Furthermore, the second defendant, Qian Asan, incited her to elope secretly. Fengdi, with her weak will, was swayed by them and, on the 12th of May this year, took her clothes and jewelry and disappeared without a trace. That same day, at 2 p.m., I suddenly received a letter from Yang, filled with absurd and baseless claims. After reading it, I reported it to the police station and posted advertisements in search of her, but without any results. Later, I received a letter from Dai Jien, a lawyer representing Yang, stating that Yang had already cohabitated with Fengdi, but the address was not clear. I immediately went to lawyer Dai's office to negotiate, but he instead advised me to sign an agreement acknowledging Yang as my son-in-law. However, I am nearing the age of knowing my fate and only have this one daughter to rely on in my old age. Yang already has a wife and children. He is clearly seducing a girl under the age of 20, and his actions constitute a crime under Article 257 of the Criminal Law, without a doubt. Moreover, Qian Asan had previously incited her to elope and provided methods for doing so, constituting a crime under Article 258 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, I am filing this lawsuit, requesting that they be arrested and punished according to the law, and that the defendants be ordered to hand over Fengdi to me and return the stolen clothes, etc. After reviewing the complaint, the court approved the request and issued summonses. Yesterday morning, judge Cheng Shangfeng ascended to the third court of the High Court and conducted a preliminary hearing. The defendants did not appear, but lawyer Chen Wenxiang appeared in court and requested a postponement. Judge Cheng verified the report, questioned the plaintiff, and ordered a postponement for a later hearing.

Tailor Covets Neighbor's Adopted Daughter-in-Law

▲ Attempted Affair Ends in Frustration and Rage

▲ Mother and Daughter-in-Law Severely Wounded

Cao Er, a 44-year-old road worker from Tongzhou, rented a rear flat at No. 15 Tanjiabang, Jiangwan Road. His wife, Mrs. Li, was 42 years old. His son, Xiao Bing, was 20 years old and also a road worker. They also had an adopted daughter-in-law, Ms. Ma, who was only 15 years old. The family of four relied on the father and son's hard labor for a meager living. Their landlord, Chen Gengquan, was a local tailor, 22 years old, unmarried, and living alone. He often saw the adopted daughter-in-law, Ms. Ma, who had a slight beauty and a small-town charm, and therefore, the idea of coveting her arose spontaneously. When Cao Er and Xiao Bing were not at home, he would often flirt with Ms. Ma, intending to seduce her. Over time, Cao Er discovered this and urgently wanted to move. He recently canceled the lease with Chen. Unexpectedly, Gengquan harbored insidious intentions, immediately falsely claiming that your wife still owes several yuan, quickly settling it will allow you to move. Mrs. Li listened to the words, started theorizing with her, and verbal arguments occurred. Yesterday, both sides invited neighbors to listen and judge, and Lu Zhonglian came forward to mediate, and the matter was settled. When Cao and his son were moving furniture, Mrs. Li was busy cooking. Chen saw an opportunity to take advantage of and immediately grabbed the arm of the adopted daughter-in-law, Ms. Ma, forcibly pulling her into the room, intending to commit indecency. Ms. Ma was greatly frightened and called out loudly. Her mother-in-law heard the alarm and arrived. Chen, upon seeing Mrs. Li, was like meeting an enemy on a narrow road. He immediately grabbed a kitchen knife and slashed Mrs. Li ten times on the head, back, and arms. The adopted daughter-in-law saw her mother-in-law covered in blood and shouted for help. Chen then rushed over and slashed the adopted daughter-in-law, Ms. Ma, more than ten times on the head, causing blood to splatter, a tragic sight to behold. Gengquan, seeing that he had caused such a disaster, suddenly contemplated suicide. He went into the room and immediately took off his pants belt and hanged himself. People came forward to rescue him while reporting to the Fifth District, Third Precinct Public Security Bureau, ordering the police to come and detain Chen at the precinct. After the chief interrogated him, he ordered him to be detained and sent to the Zhabei Judicial Section for review. The injured woman was ordered to be sent to Tongren Hospital in police car No. 3022 and then transferred to Guangren Hospital for treatment. It is said that the adopted daughter-in-law, Ms. Ma, was injured in two places on her skull, and her condition was not light.

Chinese National Invents Mosquito Repellent

Mr. Zeng Ziyun, who had studied chemistry in Europe for a long time, recognizing that mosquito repellent is an indispensable item in the summer but imported products are too expensive, meticulously researched and manufactured "Flying God" brand mosquito repellent, which also kills ants, flies, fleas, and the like, to meet the needs of society. Preparation for a Domestic Galvanized Iron Sheet Factory

It is found that galvanized iron sheet is an essential item for construction, with annual imports exceeding 600,000 piculs. Initially, it came from the United Kingdom, followed by Germany and the United States competing to contend. Recently, the Japanese imitated the manufacturing, and within three years, they unexpectedly became dominant. The goods from the United Kingdom, the United States, and Germany were all crowded out. In the national market, Japanese goods account for sixty to seventy percent. Currently, Mr. Wang Gechen, general manager of China Steel Products Company, and important figures in the iron industry, in view of this, have united with comrades to initiate China Galvanized Iron Manufacturing Co., Ltd., to establish a factory in Shanghai to manufacture galvanized iron sheet, with a capital of 300,000 yuan in national currency. They will first build the first factory, with an annual output of about 200,000 piculs of galvanized iron, which can reduce imports by one-third. In the future, they will gradually expand to achieve self-reliance. The raw materials required, except for black iron sheet, which the country cannot manufacture yet, will be temporarily ordered from the Tin Kingdom. The remaining sulfuric acid, hydrochloric acid, white alkali, and tin will all be domestic products. At a time when the anti-Japanese goods trend is in full swing, this self-made factory is a fundamental solution for crowding out Japanese goods. Those with aspirations, why not join in?

Hat-Snatching Thieves in the Min Guo Road Area

▲ Leader Captured

Recently, a gang of bandits suddenly appeared in the Min Guo Road area of Ximen, specializing in snatching straw hats from tram passengers. Taking advantage of the fact that the tram has iron doors that close, the victims had no way to react and could only sigh in vain. For this reason, there were as many as seven reported snatchings on one day. Later, these bandits became even more rampant, even snatching the straw hats of adjutants and detectives from the headquarters and French police. Wang, the district chief of the Second District Police Station, ordered Cao Junda, the leader of the detective team, to pay attention to investigating and apprehending them. He then had the detectives disguise themselves and wait in the small alleys along Min Guo Road for these bandits. The detectives pretended to stumble and feign falling into a pit. Two bandits snatched a hat and fled, and the detectives arrested them together. They confessed that they were forced to do this due to living problems. They were sentenced to be sent to the vagrant work-study center for detention and vocational training. At the same time, Li Ada, also known as Xu Atai, was arrested on Old North Gate Min Guo Road. He was the leader, so he was sent to the District Court. After interrogation, the court ordered him to be detained and severely punished.

Fei Yuqing's Daughter Killed by Car Case

▲ Car Owner and Driver to Pay a Total of 1,500 Yuan

Fei Yuqing's daughter from Sichuan was hit and killed by a truck driven by Guo Yuchun near the Great World on Edward Road in the French Concession last month. The police station then summoned both parties to the French Court for questioning. After lawyers debated, the court ordered them to await verification and judgment on record. Yesterday was the scheduled date for the verdict, and both parties were summoned. The Chinese and Western judges ruled that the defendant driver was careless and the brake system was ineffective, making it difficult to deny culpability. The defendant and the car owner were each fined 10 yuan or detained for 5 days as a warning. The deceased in this case was also at fault, so all losses should be borne equally, estimated at 3,000 yuan. Half of the amount should be calculated, and the defendant driver and car owner jointly compensate the plaintiff for a loss of 1,500 yuan.

Opium in Egg Basket on Wuxi Boat

Zhang Yushu and Tian Jingsan, police chiefs of the Second Squad of the Water Patrol Team of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, led officers such as Xie Hongqi on a river patrol near the Central Warehouse Pier of the New Garbage Bridge in Beishi at about 1 a.m. the night before last. They spotted a Wuxi boat with City Permit No. 23984 docked on the north bank of the creek. They immediately boarded the boat to conduct an inspection for contraband. They found a bamboo basket at the rear rudder of the boat. Upon opening it, they found it contained colored eggs. Upon further inspection, the lower half contained white rice. They wondered why the white rice was stored in the basket with the colored eggs and became suspicious. They inserted an iron skewer into it, pulled it out, and smelled it. They detected the smell of opium and became even more suspicious. They then poured out all the rice and discovered a large package of opium, weighing about 50 taels. They took the boat owner, Xu Lanfen, along with the evidence, back to the squad and transferred them to the Nanshi Headquarters. During the preliminary interrogation by Xu, the chief of the headquarters, Xu Lanfen, a 32-year-old from Wuxi, confessed that the bamboo basket was brought to the boat by a tea servant named Asheng from the Shanghai office of the Litae Textile Company of Taicang, North City, who entrusted him to take it to Taicang and deliver it to the Litae Textile Company for inspection. He really did not know that there was opium hidden in it. Since the case involved carrying opium, which violated the prohibition regulations, he was ordered to submit a formal statement to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

He sent a letter to Mr. Chen Liting, Secretary of the Branch, expressing his intention to resign. The original letter is as follows: "Dear Mr. Liting, I have recently read the Shanghai newspaper report of July 21st, which listed the names of the Chinese representatives attending this year's Pacific International Academic Society conference, and I was dismayed to find my name included.

I have absolutely no research on the various issues to be discussed at this conference and would be unable to adequately serve as a representative. I would be grateful if you could convey this sentiment to the committee members and select another capable person. With utmost respect, I wish you peace. Sincerely, Yang Quan, July 22nd."
